<div id="review_1089050146" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089050146" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10697179-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549097p2/10697179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089050146?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/10697179-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780307456236" href="/book/show/14739137-snuff">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089050146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5489603225772399681">This book was a disaster. I don't understand why this book exists at all. I don't know why it was published, why anyone thought it would be a good idea, and why I bothered to read it.<br/><br/>This is the first time in my life a book has made me question reading. It made me question why we read and why people write. If this is the kind of stuff being published, why do I read. I get nothing from this. No benefit and no education. I don't know why reading and writing has become such a big industry when this</span>
  <span id="freeText5489603225772399681" style="display:none">This book was a disaster. I don't understand why this book exists at all. I don't know why it was published, why anyone thought it would be a good idea, and why I bothered to read it.<br /><br />This is the first time in my life a book has made me question reading. It made me question why we read and why people write. If this is the kind of stuff being published, why do I read. I get nothing from this. No benefit and no education. I don't know why reading and writing has become such a big industry when this is all we have to show for it. It's really an embarrassment to the literary world and I personally didn't enjoy questioning why I bother to read.<br /><br />Now, I might have felt a bit different about this book had it created some sort of awareness to the realities of the porn industry. There are so many books lately creating awareness to mental health, diseases and cancer, abuse, etc. I thought you know that maybe this would create awareness about the porn industry and maybe break some of the taboos surrounding it. This did neither of those. I didn't really find it to be groundbreaking and give people a new take on porn, I actually saw it as doing the exact opposite. It makes them out to look like disgusting gross people who have nothing else in the world. I've never been on a porn set, never been in porn, have very little knowledge of how porn actually works, so maybe I am wrong here, but I feel like this was a kind of crude depiction of the industry. I can't even really tell if this book was offensive at all because it was so poorly written. <br /><br />The writing was horrible. It's clustered, confusing, and grammatically terrible. Things like "I'm touching the necklace Cassie <b>gived</b> me" and "<b>don't lets</b> be coy." Also, he had this habit of giving some weird fact and ending it with "true fact." Got old really fast. Maybe this is a usual thing for Palahniuk or his signature or something but I really was underwhelmed with the writing from a man I have heard so much about,<br /><br />This is a completely sorry excuse for a plot. Mostly because, there isn't one. Okay so you have 600 men waiting to have sex with a porn star and you get to hear from 3 of those men. That's not really what I'd call a A+ plot. It's quite lacking. There are 600 guys and you chose to focus on 3 of them? I mean I get it because of the connection between 2 of them, but why did he include guy 137? Plus why did this have to turn into a weird incestuous sort of plot? Having one of the 600 be her son and another of the 600 be her sons father just was weird. Like this brings an already messed up family dynamic into the most messed up scenario. Not to mention you have Guy 600 aka baby daddy urging his son to have sex with his mom, and later urging him to kill his mom. I really don't get it. Then there were useless beauty tips thrown in which I really didn't see the point to. They just seemed to mostly add length to this already short book.<br /><br />I feel like Palahniuk really only wrote this book because he wanted to show how creative he is at naming porn movies. There were at least 2 porn titles a page. It was excessive and useless to the "plot". I've never read a Palahniuk book before. I'd heard great things because he's the creator of Fight Club (which I've never seen the movie either) so I expected greatness from this man. I was let down like I've never been let down before.<br /><br />This was my first... and last Palahniuk book. He's really not my type of author if this is what he considers publishable material. <br /><br /><b>Book Challenge book # 31 - A Book With Bad Reviews</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5489603225772399681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2685591944?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Armand" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Armand" href="/user/show/45716474-armand">Armand</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45716474-armand?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2685591944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17413460055829713202">A still bankable pornstar slowly inching past her prime goes for one last shot at fame. She's got 600 guys primed to run a train on her in a magnum opus that will decidedly break smut records, aptly entitled <i>World Whore Three: The Whore To End All Whores</i>. If she's going out, she's gonna do so with a (gang)bang. And in a production of this scale with so much hanging in the balance, can murder be far behind? The reasonable answer to that is "prolly not", but this is a bonkers Palahniuk book, so ye</span>
  <span id="freeText17413460055829713202" style="display:none">A still bankable pornstar slowly inching past her prime goes for one last shot at fame. She's got 600 guys primed to run a train on her in a magnum opus that will decidedly break smut records, aptly entitled <i>World Whore Three: The Whore To End All Whores</i>. If she's going out, she's gonna do so with a (gang)bang. And in a production of this scale with so much hanging in the balance, can murder be far behind? The reasonable answer to that is "prolly not", but this is a bonkers Palahniuk book, so yeah we're prepping some body bags.<br /><br />It's a thoroughly enjoyable read. What seems like a tawdry plot unfolds its complex layers as the story goes by, and as one explores the twisted history of the characters one begins to grasp what's really at stake here. I've rarely encountered a book that opens with a bunch of sordid characters that I initially found pitiful/distasteful, but who I ended up rooting for. The book is big on redemption without being cheesy or self-indulgent.<br /><br /><i>Snuff</i> is replete with Palahniuk's trademark ironic and irreverent style, and his powers are on full display here. The oft-dropped trivia (on porn stars, historic whores, gangs, etc) do not get tiring - they even add spice to the story. It gets an 8/10 from me, or 4 seedy, electric stars out of 5.</span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Chuck Palahniuk fans.  Fans of Boogie Nights.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer15408243571947866927">As a Chuck Palahniuk fan, I was disappointed. It's got all the usual elements of a Chuck P. novel. Dark humor, gross material, oddball characters, and plenty of plot twists, but it's a let down after the superior Haunted and Rant.<br/><br/>It's very short. In fact, a shorter version might have made a great story in Haunted. And after the mind bending sci-fi of Rant, it seems like a far less ambitious novel. It's not bad, but it reads like something that Palahniuk did as a side project while working on som</span>
  <span id="freeText15408243571947866927" style="display:none">As a Chuck Palahniuk fan, I was disappointed. It's got all the usual elements of a Chuck P. novel. Dark humor, gross material, oddball characters, and plenty of plot twists, but it's a let down after the superior Haunted and Rant.<br /><br />It's very short. In fact, a shorter version might have made a great story in Haunted. And after the mind bending sci-fi of Rant, it seems like a far less ambitious novel. It's not bad, but it reads like something that Palahniuk did as a side project while working on something bigger and better.<br /><br />Save your money and get it from the library or wait for the paperback. Fans of Chuck will find it worth reading, but it's not worth the full hardback price at less than 200 pages.</span>

<div id="review_23296009" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23296009" />
    <a title="OutlawPoet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/245365-outlawpoet"><img alt="OutlawPoet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600195942p2/245365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23296009?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="OutlawPoet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="OutlawPoet" href="/user/show/245365-outlawpoet">OutlawPoet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23296009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14078067338218708208">Okay, I can't jump on the Snuff hate train. This wasn't the best book, but it's really not a bad offering at all.<br/><br/>Basic premise - an aging porn star goes for one last hurrah - a 600 man gang bang. However, many of the people involved, including the aging starlet herself, think that this last movie just might kill her.<br/><br/>The author let's us into the thoughts of the men standing in line for the movie and into the thoughts of one of the production people. These are very damaged people - one might say e</span>
  <span id="freeText14078067338218708208" style="display:none">Okay, I can't jump on the Snuff hate train. This wasn't the best book, but it's really not a bad offering at all.<br /><br />Basic premise - an aging porn star goes for one last hurrah - a 600 man gang bang. However, many of the people involved, including the aging starlet herself, think that this last movie just might kill her.<br /><br />The author let's us into the thoughts of the men standing in line for the movie and into the thoughts of one of the production people. These are very damaged people - one might say even more damaged than the star herself. Their stories are full of pathos - some heart rending.<br /><br />There are a few surprises in store for the reader. Unlike some other reviewers of the book, I did not see the "maternal twist" coming. LOL - guess I was a bit slow on the uptake. And the ending definitely came as a surprise to me.<br /><br />The book is full of odd trivia facts. The facts are very cool, however since they come in each of the character's chapters, the characters lose their individuality and tend to mesh into each other after a while. <br /><br />Finally, some of the reviews I've read seem to take issue about the fact that the author shows only the tarnish of the porn industry, not the glamour.<br /><br />A few years ago, I worked with people who also did porn part time. Some were actors, others worked in photography and production. Based on my conversations with them about this industry, I think that the author does as very good job of writing about the grimmer parts of the industry. The suicides, disease, and drugs that the characters speak about are all a very real part of the industry.<br /><br />Snuff gives you an unvarnished look at an industry most people don't know much about. It's a dark look, but worth the read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14078067338218708208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText194653028763149405" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380436819i/883090._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="484" height="358" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Awww too bad, I really loved <b>Fight club</b> and I was really looking forward to find some grit in this novel, sadly all I’ve read were a parody of porn titles and porn slangs that made me uncomfortable but I must say that it’s a bold move for <b>Chuck Palahniuk</b> to write a novel about <i>Porn</i>. <br><br><b><i>“Six hundred dudes. To write about how the porn industry works and as to why it never gets old, in fact it’s a growing industry. In this novel not only women are objectified and exploited but also men, it points out the psychological aspect of the people who ended up in such business, it talks about social issues such abuse, rape and rejection. Chuck had the right elements to make this novel work but disappointingly his execution fell short of what I was hoping for and focused more on making sure he had enough porn titles we should know about… Chuck I get it okay!?!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890472277" />
    <a title="Stacy Fetters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29942945-stacy-fetters"><img alt="Stacy Fetters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573594587p2/29942945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/890472277?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy Fetters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy Fetters" href="/user/show/29942945-stacy-fetters">Stacy Fetters</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer16824093119966359815"><b>"When your agent sends you in a look-see to f**k a dead woman, you know your career’s in the toilet."</b><br/><br/>One of my favorite things about Chuck Palahniuk is that he’s not afraid to put something strange and bizarre out into the world. He loves that shock factor that his books bring to the world and I’m here breathing it in like it’s my last breath. <br/><br/>Snuff is one of my favorite books by Chuck. It’s one that gets even more bizarre every time you read it and I can’t get enough. Who would have thought a b</span>
  <span id="freeText16824093119966359815" style="display:none"><b>"When your agent sends you in a look-see to f**k a dead woman, you know your career’s in the toilet."</b><br /><br />One of my favorite things about Chuck Palahniuk is that he’s not afraid to put something strange and bizarre out into the world. He loves that shock factor that his books bring to the world and I’m here breathing it in like it’s my last breath. <br /><br />Snuff is one of my favorite books by Chuck. It’s one that gets even more bizarre every time you read it and I can’t get enough. Who would have thought a book about making a gang bang snuff film would be so entertaining? <br /><br />Thank you, Chuck, for opening my eyes up to this insanity. I loved every second of it!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Didn’t one of us on purpose set out to make a snuff movie."</i>
</b></span>

  <span id="freeText10120860274730075200" style="display:none">This one is about as palatable as purple buttercream veins on a Devils food cake erection.<br /><br />Everybody loves Cassie. Who wouldn’t love the star of movie mega hits such as Good Will Humping and Emergency Room Backdoor Dog Pile? Plus, 600 dudes later, she is about to make a world record for the ages. The problem is, it just may kill her. That’s the plan anyway.<br /><br />First off, I like Palahniuk…usually. This was definitely not my favorite of his, but a friend of mine gave me the audio book so I thought I would give it a go. Unfortunately, it was just mediocre. Nothing either character or plot wise really stood out like it should have given the subject matter. Not horrible, but not as Palahniuk as it should or could have been. 2.5 Stars<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc" href="/user/show/18218857-marc">Marc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18218857-marc?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18218857-marc?shelf=taboo-or-not-for-the-dinner-table">taboo-or-not-for-the-dinner-table</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065206924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7674390133732192438">This was solidly stuck between a 2- and a 3-star experience, but instead of opting to write a longer review touching more on what Palahniuk might have done with the book, I'm bumping it up to 3 stars and using that half-star raise to excuse myself from a long review. You read enough Chuck and it all starts to feel like a formula. He's like the Tarantino of transgressive novels. Chooses edgy subject matter, highlights contradictions inherent in contemporary life and capitalism, digresses every 8 </span>
  <span id="freeText7674390133732192438" style="display:none">This was solidly stuck between a 2- and a 3-star experience, but instead of opting to write a longer review touching more on what Palahniuk might have done with the book, I'm bumping it up to 3 stars and using that half-star raise to excuse myself from a long review. You read enough Chuck and it all starts to feel like a formula. He's like the Tarantino of transgressive novels. Chooses edgy subject matter, highlights contradictions inherent in contemporary life and capitalism, digresses every 8 pages into pop culture and science trivia that no one knows, ... it just starts to feel more like a schtick from which he's squeezed every last bit of literary juice. If you haven't read much of his work, you might get a kick out of most of this, but it starts to wear thin after a while despite a lot of humor, pathos, and poignant social commentary. I think this might be the last of his work I read. I will say, it's no small thing to pull off two-hundred pages essentially centered around 3 of the 600 guys waiting backstage to be part of a record-breaking porn filming. Maybe it's more that individual parts were quite effective, but the whole felt somewhat mashed together. I did read it in one day so I must have been mostly entertained...</span>
  <a data-text-id="7674390133732192438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_9912'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9912.The_Rules_of_Attraction"><img alt="The Rules of Attraction" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1468426907l/9912._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RLLJusBvaejs/euGSXG6LhCNO9pvzFAmqeoPysX68+x+lKBoezGggEvWX+e+hLDxxtLcEqFB3kHylEl7CLkBdg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ypGiDj4P2K4KQWjQ37SyhKNJd5NWDB1T23wODwLwsKDwt8vchVERxq1q3LEoQbhbdRaQW5iBkzSAAki+z7NCOg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk">About Chuck Palahniuk</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13206672621406715100">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’</span>
  <span id="freeText13206672621406715100" style="display:none">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’s first New York Times bestseller. Chuck’s work has always been infused with personal experience, and his next novel, <i>Lullaby</i>, was no exception. Chuck credits writing <i>Lullaby</i> with helping him cope with the tragic death of his father. <i>Diary</i> and the non-fiction guide to Portland, <i>Fugitives and Refugees</i>, were released in 2003. While on the road in support of <i>Diary</i>, Chuck began reading a short story entitled 'Guts,' which would eventually become part of the novel <i>Haunted</i>.<br /><br />In the years that followed, he continued to write, publishing the bestselling <i>Rant, Snuff, Pygmy, Tell-All, a 'remix' of Invisible Monsters, Damned</i>, and most recently, <i>Doomed</i>. <br /><br />Chuck also enjoys giving back to his fans, and teaching the art of storytelling has been an important part of that. In 2004, Chuck began submitting essays to ChuckPalahniuk.net on the craft of writing. These were 'How To' pieces, straight out of Chuck's personal bag of tricks, based on the tenants of minimalism he learned from Tom Spanbauer. Every month, a “Homework Assignment” would accompany the lesson, so Workshop members could apply what they had learned. (all 36 of these essays can currently be found on The Cult's sister-site, LitReactor.com).<br /><br />Then, in 2009, Chuck increased his involvement by committing to read and review a selection of fan-written stories each month. The best stories are currently set to be published in <i>Burnt Tongues</i>, a forthcoming anthology, with an introduction written by Chuck himself. <br /><br />His next novel, <i>Beautiful You</i>, is due out in October 2014.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13206672621406715100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
